Annotated Checklist of Lichens and Allied Fungi of New England

Conventions Used in this Checklist

Accepted Species list
Genus names:
	All caps and bolded for those with accepted species; all caps and not bolded for rest
	Follow Esslinger 2021 for accepted names, including spelling, not Index Fungorum
	Author abbreviations are those used in Index Fungorum but with no space after periods
	In alphabetical order
 
Listed below are the sections displayed in order for each accepted species description*
1. Species names:
	Accepted species bolded in an alphabetical list under genus, with genus name not repeated; most but not all species accepted or excluded by Esslinger 2021 are treated similarly in this checklist; exceptions are noted in the comments section of the specimen citations
	Species with synonyms or those not accepted are in an alphabetical, italicized list immediately following the accepted list for each genus 
	Many but not all excluded species further explained in the Excluded Species list following the main checklist and Herbarium abbreviations
	Author abbreviations are those used in Index Fungorum but with no spaces after periods
	* precedes accepted species names known to be lichenicolous fungi
	+ precedes accepted species thought to be allied fungi (nonlichenized fungi in groups usually studied by lichenologists or species collected by well-known lichenologists); if no symbol precedes the species names, that species is assumed to be lichenized
	Preceding symbols are only used for accepted species, not for synonymized or excluded species
	A vertical line follows each accepted species name, setting it off from the specimen citations that follow
	With rare exceptions, only validly published names (In Index Fungorum) are cited
2. Specimen citations
	Order of states cited is from most boreal to least boreal: ME, NH, VT, MA, RI, CT
	Source of most citations is CLH (Consortium of Lichen Herbaria); also, the New York Botanical Garden (NYBG) website and published articles
	The citations for each state generally is the earliest specimen known that has good information, such as collector and year collected; preference is given to those with more recent annotations unless the identification of the species is straightforward
	Format for each specimen citation is usually as follows: [two letter state abbreviation bolded, then colon], herbarium abbreviation], then the following in parentheses [collector’s last name], [year collected or “s.d.”], [locality information, if deemed appropriate], [type (bolded) if known], [annotatiion if present; phrase “det by” used for both verifications and re-determinations]; if there would be ambiguity as to who collected the specimen using just the last name, a first name initial was added
	More locality information is usually given for rare species than for common ones
	For each species one specimen selected for full citation information, including herbarium number or collector number, and locality information at least to county; this full citation is for well identified specimens, often notable for location, date of collection, unusual substrate, or other attributes
	If a species has collections later than 1945, at least one will be cited; no such collections cited means there was none known
	Usually only one citation per state; if two records are cited, they are separated by an ampersand (&)
	If no extant specimen is known but the species is stated as being from New England or one of its states, then a reference takes the place of the herbarium abbreviation
	If a named subspecies or variety is used in Esslinger 2021, then information on that taxon is provided in the specimen citations to the extent known
3. Earliest publication of a species being from New England
	Following the specimen citations is a reference, if known, that first stated a particular species is known from New England or its states; if a reference mentions that a species is found in northern US or northeastern North America, it is not considered to have stated it was from New England
	For early publications a judgment needs to be made if the species name is the same as its use currently; often that is not the case; if the name used in the publication is different from its current name, the name actually used is given 
	If no publication is known stating that the species is from New England, a statement “new report for N.E.” is made, and this is highlighted in light blue
	If the name in the checklist or its synonym is not present in Esslinger 2021, the statement “not on the N.A. Checklist (Esslinger 2021)” is highlighted in bright green
4. Rarity information
	If a species in the checklist has been found in more than 10 sites in New England (each more than 1 mile apart), then there is nothing listed in the rarity section that immediately following the reference citation
	Species known only from records in the New England region before 1946 are considered only historical and designated with a bolded *RH* (R stands for a regional list) no matter how many sites were known historically
	Species known from 1 to 5 records in New England region are shown as a bolded *R1* 
	Species known from 6 to 10 records in New England are shown as a bolded *R2*
	Species known from more than 10 sites but are deemed of conservation concern because of few recent records or occupying only specialized habitats are designated as a bolded *R3*
	Following the RH, R1, R2, or R3 designations the number of sites known is listed in parentheses.
5. Comments
	Set off in square brackets
	Includes further information on nomenclatural issues or other issues deemed important

Synonym and Excluded Species list 
	Placed Immediately after the accepted species list for each genus; species names are italicized and in alphabetical order
	If the authority for the synonym was from Esslinger 2021, no source is given; most of the synonyms listed are from Esslinger 2021
	If the authority for the synonym came from another source, it is provided in parentheses after the synonym
	An attempt was made to include all valid names said to be from New England in Tuckerman 1882 and 1888, Willey 1890 and 1892; Evans and Meyrowitz 1926, Fink 1935, and Degelius 1940, as well as more recent works, either on the accepted list or on the list of synonyms and excluded species 

Herbarium abbreviations list
	Alphabetical by herbarium abbreviation
	Most from Consortium of Lichen Herbaria (CLH) website; rest from Holmgren et al. 1990

Excluded Species list
	A subset of the excluded species listed in the Synonym and Excluded Species list is listed in an alphabetical list by its currently accepted name per Esslinger 2021 or Index Fungorum
	Each species listed has Information on where the excluded species name was found (e.g., a specimen in CLH, or a published reference), what its assessment is (usually identity uncertain, or presumed misidentification), and sometimes why it is being excluded


ABROTHALLUS De Not.

Abrothallus lobariae (Diederich & Etayo) Diederich & Ertz | ME: MIN #906737 (Hawksworth, 2001, Hancock Co., on Lobaria pulmonaria); Seaward et al. 2017, as Phoma lobariae; *R1* (1 site)
Abrothallus microspermus Tul. | ME: MIN #872871 (Sullivan, 1983, Hancock Co., on Punctelia rudecta, det M.Cole) & NY #1818680 (Harris, 2014, Washington Co., Roque I., on Flavoparmelia caperata, as its anamorph, Vouauxiomyces truncatus); Cole & Hawksworth 2001; *R1* (2 sites)
Abrothallus parmeliarum (Sommerf.) Arnold | ME: FH (Merrill, 1910) & NY #2467726 (Harris, 2016, Washington Co., on Parmelia sulcata); NH: NY (Tuckerman, 1843, on Parmelia saxatilis); VT: VT (Dutton, 1926); MA: FH (Willey, 1800s); CT: DUKE (Hale, 1949); Tuckerman 1888, as Buellia parmeliarum
Abrothallus santessonii (D.Hawksw) Suija, D.Hawksw. & Pérez-Ort. | ME: NY #2971103 (Harris, 2007, Washington Co., Great Wass I., on Platismatia glauca, det R.Harris 2019); MA: NY (Buck, 1995, Berkshire Co., Mt. Greylock, on Platismatia glauca); Seaward et al. 2017, as Abrothallus cetrariae I.Kotte and Vouauxiomyces santessonii D.Hawksw.; not on the N.A. Checklist (Esslinger 2021); *R1* (5 sites) [Seaward et al. 2017 assumed that V. santessonii was the anamorph of A. cetrariae, but Suija et al. 2018 show that A. cetrariae and A. santessonii are two separate species, differing, e.g., in the length of their conidia]
Abrothallus tulasnei M.S.Cole & D.Hawksw. | ME: Hb Hawksworth (Hawksworth, s.d., Washington or Hancock Co.); Seaward et al. 2017 *R1* (1 site)
Abrothallus usneae Rabenh. | ME: NY #2971148 (Harris, 2007, Washington Co., Great Wass I., on Usnea cornuta); new report for N.E.; *R1* (2 sites)
Abrothallus cetrariae I.Kotte %% A. parmeliarum (Esslinger 2021), but also see Excluded Species list for A. cetrariae
Abrothallus oxysporus Tul. %% Nesolechia oxyspora
Abrothallus smithii Tul. %% A. parmeliarum (Index Fungorum)

Excluded Species
Abrothallus cetrariae Kotte (Seaward et al. 1917); no specimens found from New England; Seaward et al. 2017 listed Vouauxiomyces santessonii as the anamorph of Abrothallus cetrariae, but A. cetrariae and A. santessonii are now known to be two separate species (Suija et al. 2018)
Acarospora cervina A.Massal. (CLH, 22 specimens, most recent 1912); misidentifications per Knudsen & Kocourková 2020
Acarospora citrina (Taylor) Zahlbr. (CLH, 1 specimen from CT); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Acarospora glaucocarpa (Ach.) Körb. (CLH, 37 specimens; Fink 1935) per Knudsen et al. 2020, not in N.A.
Acarospora heufleriana Körb. (CLH, 1 specimen, from ME); identity not certain, far from rest of geographical distribution in western N.A, and substrate highly atypical
Acarospora schleicheri (Ach.) A.Massal. (CLH, Hall 1862 specimen at F identified by B. Fink); location presumably mislabeled as MA because “high alpine” habitat does not exist in MA
Acarospora xanthophana (Nyl.) Jatta: (CLH, 1 specimen from CT; Evans & Meyrowitz 1926); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Acolium sessile (Pers.) Arnold (CLH, one specimen from MA collected by Mann in 1863; 
Fink 1935); note on specimen at FH: “NOT C. sessile”; identity uncertain 
Acolium viridulum Schaer. (CLH, 2 specimens, Pringle and G.Merrill); status uncertain; these are the only two specimens of the species in N.A. in CLH
Acrocordia gemmata (Ach.) A.Massal. (CLH, 19 specimens); per Harris 1995, does not occur in North America except in Florida
Ainoa mooreana (Carroll) Lumbsch & I.Schmitt (CLH, 1 MA specimen); misidentification for N.A (Esslinger 2021)
Alectoria chalybeiformis (L.) Gray (CLH, 34 specimens; Tuckerman 1882, as A. jubata, var. chelybeiformis; Fink 1935); %% B. fuscescens, but for N.E. specimens a misapplied name for B. furcellata
Alectoria imshaugii Brodo & D.Hawksw. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification
Alectoria jubata (L.) Ach. (CLH, 66 specimens); identity not certain; could be a number of pendent species of Bryoria
Allantoparmelia alpicola (Th.Fr.) Essl.(CLH, 3 specimens; Bowley 1978, as Parmelia alpicola); identity uncertain
Amandinea leucomela (Imshaug) P.May & Sheard (CLH, 7 specimens from MA); identity not certain, location far from range of other specimens
Anaptychia runcinata (With.) J.R.Laundon (CLH, 18 specimens); not found in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Anthracothecium pachycheilum (Tuck.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 1 specimen, from NH); far from rest of distribution in N.A.; presumed misidentification
Arthonia abietina Willey (CLH, 1 Willey specimen from MA: Willey 1892); not in Index Fungorum; presumably a name not validly published, as also suggested by Willey’s comment (1892); “.., as I had distinguished in herb, ...”
Arthonia albovirescens Nyl. (CLH, 1 Calkins specimen); identity and/or provenance not certain; far from the distribution of other records of this species in SE US
Arthonia biformis (Flörke) Schaer. (CLH, 4 specimens, from NH, VT & MA); Willey 1890 considers it a European species, but it is included in Willey 1892; Fink 1935 lists it as a synonym of A. byssacea; not in Esslinger 2021; probably a misapplied name for A. byssacea
Arthonia calcicola Nyl. (CLH, 1 specimen, Merrill, 1914, ME); identity uncertain; only known specimen with this name in N.A.
Arthonia cytisi A.Massal. (Fink 1935 synonymizes Arthonia hibernica and A. excipienda Nyl. with A. cytisi and notes it has been found in MA); R. Sundin, in a 1999 annotation on a Willey specimen at FH from MA (and identified as A. hibernica ), asserts that this specimen was “not A. cytisi”; in addiition, CLH does not support the synonymy of A. hibernica and A. excipienda with A. cytisi, and no specimens labeled A. cytisi have been found from N.E. in CLH
Arthonia polymorpha Ach. (CLH, 2 specimens from VT collected in 1850s); Willey 1890 says the species is tropical extending to southern US; probably misidentifications
Arthonia rubrocincta G.Merr. ex Grube & Lendemer (CLH, 1 Merrill specimen incorrectly said to be from ME, on Palmetto, a plant that does not grow in ME)
Arthonia saxatilis Vain. (CLH, 1 Merrill specimen from ME); presumably a misidentification by G.K.Merrill, who noted its hymenium looked more like a Buellia than an Arthonia; not in Willey 1890 or Esslinger 2021 
Arthonia vagans Almq. (CLH, 1 Willey specimen, the only specimen from N.A.); presumed misidentification; not in Willey 1890 or Esslinger 2021
Arthonia velata f. develata Nyl. (CLH, 1 VT specimen) ; identity uncertain (Esslinger 2021)
Arthopyrenia salicis A.Massal. (CLH, 3 Willey specimens); identity uncertain; Harris 1995 states ”Position uncertain”
Arthopyrenia macrocarpa (Körb.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 1 specimen); misidentification for N.A. (Esslnger 2021)
Arthothelium ceraceum (Fée) A.Massal. (CLH, 1 specimen, Merrill, 1912); FH labels this as the type of A. ceraceum, but that makes little sense, since Fée described the species in 1837; also, Merrill’s handwritten name says “ Arthonia (Arthothelium) cerasi Merl., sp. nov.”, which suggests that he was describing a different species, one not validly published
Arthothelium distendens (Nyl.) Müll.Arg. (CLH, 1 specimen from ME); far from rest of the species distribution in extreme SE US and West Indies; presumed misidentification
Arthothelium hallii (Tuck.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 1 specimen from MA collected by Sherwood in 1978 and identified as “cfr. hallii”); identity uncertain; few collections of this species are known, all from a small area in the mid-west; description of species (Willey 1890) apparently based on one specimen
Arthothelium subastroideum (Anzi) Rehm (CLH, 1 specimen); misreading of handwritten label (Arthonia astroidella Nyl.); not a validly published species
Aspicilia caesiopruinosa (H.Magn.) J.W.Thomson (CLH, 2 specimen at CONN from VT and CT); presumed misidentification of this arctic species
Bacidia assulata (Körb.) Vězda (CLH, 1 Willey specimen from MA labeled Biatora effusa var. arceutina misfiled with this name)
Bacidia coprodes (Körb.) Lettau (CLH, 2 specimens, from VT and CT, collected in 2010 and 2012 are filed under this name, following Llop & Ekman 2007; however Ekman 2014 reversed his earlier decision to synonymize Bacidia granosa into Bacidia coprodes and said that there was only one true B. coprodes he knows of in North America, in SD, with the inference that the rest are B. granosa)
Bacidia incompta (Borrer ex Hook.) Anzi (CLH, 5 specimens; Willey 1892); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Bacidia ophiospora (Hellb.) Th.Fr. (CLH, 1 specimen from ME collected by Norton in 1915 and identified by G. K. Merrill); name is not in Ekman 1996 or Esslinger 2021; presumed misidentification
Bacidia rosellizans S.Ekman (CLH, 4 specimens, from ME and VT, filed under this name); Ekman 2009, in describing this species, only cited 3 specimens from North America, the same ones he had determined as B. rosella in Ekman 1996, and none were from New England; Ekman 1996 states that most species labeled B. rosellizans are other species
Bacidia viridescens (A.Massal.) Hellb. (CLH, 1 specimen labeled Lecidea viridescens on packet from MA collected by Faxon in 1883); name entered incorrectly into CLH 
Bactrospora homalotropa (Nyl.) Gilenstam (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; a European species not yet confirmed in N.A.; not in Esslinger 2021
Biatora atrorubens (Fr.) G.Merr. (CLH, 4 specimens, all collected by G. K. Merrill); status uncertain; no other N.A. records; name not in Esslinger 2021
Biatora chloropholis Tuck. ex E.Michener (CLH, 2 specimens of Frost); status uncertain; no other N.A. records; name not in Esslinger 2021
Biatora cladoniscum Willey (CLH, 2 specimens; Willey 1892; Fink 1935); apothecia of Pycnothelia papillaria (Esslinger 2021)
Biatora effusa (Sm.) Hepp (CLH, one Willey specimen from MA); identity not certain but per Ekman 1996 Bacidina assulata (a synonym of B.effusa) has only been found in N.A. from Oklahoma
Biatora epigena Nyl. (CLH, one Frost specimen from VT); identity not known; name not in Index Fungorum 
Biatora frostii Tuck. (CLH, three Frost specimens from VT); identity not known; name not in Index Fungorum 
Biatora helvola Körb. ex Hellbom (19 specimens in CLH); Printzen & Tønsberg 1999 stated that all N.A. records with this name were probably misidentifications of other species, although since then the species has been found in Alaska (Spribille et al. 2010)
Biatora mollis (Wahlenb.) Arnold (Tuckerman 1888, as Biatora rivulosa var. mollis, in NH); %% Fuscidea mollis but Fryday 2008 says not in northeastern N.A.
Biatora papillariae Willey (CLH, 3 specimens; Willey 1892; Fink 1935); apothecia of Pycnothelia papillaria (Esslinger 2021)
Biatora planata Willey: (CLH, 1 specimen at US labeled "type", but it appears never to have been validly published because "ined" is also written on sheet) ; the name is not in Willey 1892, nor in Index Fungorum
Biatora rivulosa (Ach.) Fr. (CLH, 5 specimens; Tuckerman 1888); %% Fuscidea cyathoides, but that species is not in N.A. (Fryday 2008)
Biatorella fossarum (Dufour) Th.Fr. (CLH, 1 Willey specimen); specimen is actually from Illinois
Biatorina intermixta (Nyl.) Kieff. %% Megalaria intermixta (Index Fungorum), but see Excluded Species list
Bilimbia microcarpa (Th.Fr.) Th.Fr. (CLH, 2 specimens); status uncertain; substrate does not match that for other records of this relatively rare species 
Blastenia ferruginea (Huds.) Th.Fr. (CLH, 95 specimens, the latest 1956; LaGreca et al. 2005); current concept of this species (Wetmore 2007) has changed greatly since the 1800s and 1900s, when it was much broader than now; in NA now thought to be is a western species restricted to bark and wood and found currently only as far east as Ontario (Brinker 2020)
Bogoriella thelena (Ach.) Aptroot & Lücking (CLH, 22 specimens); not found in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Brigantiaea leucoxantha (Spreng.) R.Sant. & Hafellner (Fink 1935, as Lopadium leucoxanthum, ME); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in SE US and south
Brodoa atrofusca (Schaer.) Goward (CLH, 1 specimen from NH as Parmelia encausta annotated by K.Ohlsson in 1972 as Hypogymnia atrofusca); N.A. reports are probably misidentifications of Brodoa oroarctica (Esslinger 2021)
Brodoa intestiniformis (Vill.) Goward (CLH, 1 specimen); N.A. reports are misidentifications of Brodoa oroarctica (Esslinger 2021)
Bryoria glabra (Motyka) Brodo & D.Hawksw. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; probably a misapplied name for Bryoria fuscescens
Buellia conspirans (Nyl.) Vain. (CLH, 19 specimens, from CT and VT, most recent specimen collected in 1949); per Imshaug 1951, found in Florida and Gulf states; presumed misidentifications
Buellia pullata Tuck. (Tuckerman 1888, MA); identity uncertain; Bungartz et al. 2007 state that this species is distinct from Amandinea punctata, but MA is far from the major location of the species in southern CA
Buellia stellulata (Taylor) Mudd (CLH, 1 Willey MA specimen); per Imshaug 1951, a European and western NA species; probably a misidentification
Buellia trypethelii Tuck. (CLH, 4 specimens, one identified as Karschia (now Rhizodiscina) lignyota by J.Hafellner in 1976); presumed misidentification of this southern species.
Buellia virescens Willey (CLH, 1 specimen, a type specimen from Fall River MA collected by H.Willey in 1876); annotated by H.Imshaug in 1951 as Lecidea sp.; not in Index Fungorum
Calicium albidum (Körb.) Nyl. (CLH, 1 Willey specimen from NH); per Index Fungorum, nom. illegit.
Calicium corynellum (Ach.) Ach. (CLH, 1 recent corticolous specimen from ME); presumed misidentification,; far from rest of N.A. distribution; normally saxicolous
Calicium notarisii (Tul.) M.Prieto & Wedin (CLH, 7 specimens all at the same herbarium); appears to be a mistaken synonymy for specimens originally labeled Acolium, Cyphelium, or Trachylia tigillare
Calicium phaeomelaenum Tuck. (CLH, 1 Tuckerman specimen from NH); identity not certain
Calicium praestantius Nyl. (CLH, 1 Willey specimen from NH); identity not certain
Calicium rhois (Berk. & M.A.Curtis) Farl. (CLH, 3 Farlow specimens, ME & NH); identity not certain 
Calogaya biatorina (A.Massal.) Arup, Frödén & Søchting (CLH, 1 record, ME by Plitt); far from the rest of the distribution in N.A. (western); identification uncertain
Calogaya decipiens (Arnold) Arup, Frödén & Søchting (CLH, 11 specimens, all collected by Dutton in VT); identification uncertain; far from rest of its N.A. distribution in western N.A.
Calogaya lobulata (Flörke) Arup, Frödén & Søchting (CLH, 2 Howe specimens, one from RI and one from MA determined in Rudolph 1955, as Gasparrinia lobulata (Flörke) Mereschk.); far from rest of N.A. distribution of Iowa west and north; identification uncertain
Caloplaca cinnabarina (Ach.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 31 specimens; Tuckerman 1882; Willey 1892); Per Wetmore & Kärnefelt 1999 this name has been misapplied widely (e.g., for C. subsoluta), but in greater N.A. it is restricted to southern US, Mexico, and the Caribbean
Caloplaca diphyodes (Nyl.) Jatta (CLH, 1 Howe specimen from MA, originally labeled Blastenia ferruginea var. discolor (Willey) comb. nov.); filed under a mistaken synonym
Caloplaca fulva (Schwein.) Halsey (CLH, 2 Tuckerman specimens from MA); identity uncertain; these are the only two specimens in N.A.; nom. illegit. per Index Fungorum
Caloplaca kamczatica (Savicz) Savicz (CLH, 1 specimen from MA annotated by Rudolph in 1955 as Blastenia vicaria (H.Magn.) Rud.); presumed misidentification since all other specimens are from the Pacific Northwest
Caloplaca ochracea (Schaer.) Flagey (CLH, 1 specimen from CT); annotated “too immature to determine” by Rudolph in 1955
Caloplaca oregona H.Magn.(CLH, 2 Lindblom specimens from ME); identity uncertain per specimen label
Caloplaca schaereri (Flörke) Zahlbr.(CLH 1 Cummings specimen from MA); misidentification; annotated as Caloplaca scopularis by C. Wetmore in 1996 
Calvitimela armeniaca (DC.) Hafellner (CLH, 1 NH specimen collected at 945 m on Mt. Monadnock in 1959); far from rest of distribution in the arctic and western mountains; identity uncertain
Candelaria laciniosa (Nyl.) Kieff. (CLH, 13 specimens); uncertain status, but most or all are probably C. concolor
Candelariella arctica (Körb.) R.Sant. (CLH, 1 specimen from VT collected in 1935; Fink 1935, as C. crenulata); far from rest of distribution in the arctic and western mountains; identity uncertain
Canoparmelia caroliniana (Nyl.) Elix & Hale (CLH, 1 Frost specimen from VT at FH); far from the rest of the distribution of the species in SE US south; presumed misidentification
Catillaria contristans (Nyl.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 1 specimen; Miller et al. 2005, Fryday 2006, Hinds et al. 2009); a misidentification (Svensson & Fryday 2022)
Catillochroma endochroma (Fée) Kalb (CLH, 1 specimen, VT, 1920); far from rest of distribution of the species in Florida south; presumed misidentification
Cetrariella commixta (Nyl.) A.Thell & Kärnefelt (CLH, 60 specimens; Tuckerman 1882, Fink 1935; Thomson 1984, as Cetraria commixta); specimens examined from N.E. named Cetraria fahlunensis have all proved to be Melanelia hepatizon; misapplied synonymy of Cetraria fahlunensis 
Chrismofulvea pinastri (Erichsen) Marbach (CLH, 3 specimens, all Lich. Exs. #32 (first series) of G. K. Merrill from Knox Co. ME), but this exsiccati has been annotated by H.Imshaug (1951, F) and R.Harris (1988, FLAS) as Buellia dialyta, a synonym of Chrismofulvea dialyta
Chrysothrix candelaris (L.) J.R.Laundon (CLH, 6 specimens from ME, VT & CT); per Harris & Ladd 2008, specimens identified as Chrysothrix candelaris in eastern N.A. are C. xanthina 
Chrysothrix flavovirens Tønsberg (CLH, 4 specimens); per Lendemer & Elix 2010, specimens identified as this species in eastern N.A. are C. chamaecyparicola
Circinaria calcarea (L.) A. Nordin, Savić & Tibell (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in western N.A.
Circinaria gibbosa (Ach.) A.Nordin, S.Savić & Tibell (CLH, 28 specimens in N.E. before 1960 and none after; Purvis et al. 1992 report that most UK specimens labeled Aspicilia gibbosa have proved to be A. caesiocinerea)
Cladonia bacilliformis (Nyl.) Sarnth. (CLH, 2 Willey specimens from southeast MA); presumed misidentification, since the species range in N.A., as presently understood, is northern and western
Cladonia bellidiflora (Ach.) Schaer. (CLH, 7 specimens from 19th and early 20th century); identification not certain; several of these seven have been annotatated as other species, such as C. cristatella, C. floerkeana, and C. coccifera, but others have not been critically evaluated
Cladonia caroliniana Tuck. (CLH, 68 specimens); identity not certain; as pointed out by Ahti (1973) many of the specimens named C. caroliniana are really C. dimorphoclada, formerly a variety of C. caroliniana, but in that publication he still believed C. caroliniana was found in Maine; later (1998), however, Ahti (pers. comm.) said he no longer believed that there were any C. caroliniana specimens from Maine; Merrill’s 1924 FH specimen that forms Sandstede’s Clad. Exs. #1471 has been annotated by S. LaGreca as C. uncialis
Cladonia ciliata Stirt. (CLH, 24 specimens); in N.E. a misapplied name for C. subtenuis
Cladonia confusa R.Sant. (CLH, 11 specimens); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021
Cladonia fimbriata var. tubaeformis (Hoffm.) Fr. (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain (Esslinger 2021)
Cladonia foliacea (Huds.) Willd. (CLH, 38 specimens; many 19th and early 20th century publications); per Esslinger 2021, misidentifications for N.A.
Cladonia glacialis Kristinsson & Ahti (CLH 1 site); misreading of C. gracilis on specimen
Cladonia graciliformis Zahlbr. (CLH, 14 specimens); not found in N.A (Esslinger 2021)
Cladonia humilis (With.) J.R.Laundon (CLH, 50 specimens; Hinds & Hinds 2007); In N.E. a misapplied name for C. conista; molecular studies of Pino-Bodas et al. 2012 show C. humilis and C. conista are separate species
Cladonia leporina Fr. (CLH, 1 record at FH from Nantucket, MA; Mish 1972); “non” per S.Hammer annotation
Cladonia macroceras (Delise) Ahti (CLH, 1 probable Tuckerman specimen from NH annotated by T.Ahti in 1972 as C. macroceras (Flörke) Ahti ined); Ahti (1980), however, changed his mind and stated that no definite specimens of C. macroceras have been found in the US outside of Alaska
Cladonia nanodes Robbins ex Sandst. (CLH, 10 specimens); per Esslinger 2021, identity uncertain
Cladonia peltasta (Ach.) Spreng. (CLH, 1 Faxon specimen from 1883); presumed misidentification; a tropical species.
Cladonia portentosa (Dufour) Coem. (CLH, 34 specimens; Evans 1930, as C. impexa); per Thomson 1967 and Evans 1944 specimens named C. impexa from eastern N.A. are most likely C. terrae-novae or C. subtenuis
Cladonia pyxioides (Wallr.) Britzelm. (CLH, 10 specimens); identity not certain
Cladonia rangiformis Hoffm. (CLH, 6 specimens); per Esslinger 2021 not in N.A.
Cladonia stricta (Nyl.) Nyl. (CLH, 4 specimens labeled C. lepidota); presumed misapplied name of specimens of C. piedmontensis. 
Cladonia subsubulata Nyl. (CLH, 38 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Cladonia transcendens (Vain.) Vain. (CLH, 1 VT specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in western N.A.
Coccotrema maritimum Brodo (CLH, 1 specimen at UC collected on the Maine coast in 2006); identity uncertain; all other reports of this have been from the Pacific Northwest
Coccocarpia pellita (Ach.) Müll.Arg. (CLH, 6 specimens); status uncertain; primarily a tropical lichens; no recent records
Coccocarpia stellata Tuck. (CLH, 1 specimen); Original label said C. cronia; current name is C. palmicola
Collema crispum (Huds.) Weber ex F.H.Wigg. (CLH, 2 Willey specimens from MA); Degelius 1954 states that this name has been misapplied to Collema bachmanianum (Fink) Degel.
Collema myochroum (Ehrh. ex Bernh.) Rabenh. (CLH, 1 specimen); probably a misidentification; not in Esslinger 2021
Coniarthonia pyrrhula (Nyl.) Grube (CLH, 4 specimens; Fink 1935); presumed misidentification; per Willey 1890 probably misapplied name for Arthonia pyrrhuliza
Coniocarpon tuckermanianum (Willey) Van den Broeck & Ertz (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; specimen from MA at MICH is labeled as co-type, but annotation by H.Willson in 1982 quoting Willey 1890 says type is from Florida
Constrictolumina lyrata (R.C.Harris) Lücking, M.P.Nelsen & Aptroot (CLH, 1 specimen) presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in N.A.
Constrictolumina malaccitula (Nyl.) Lücking, M.P.Nelsen & Aptroot (CLH, 1 specimen, from NH); presumed misidentification; far from the rest of its distribution in extreme SE US and West Indies
Cornicularia normoerica (Gunn.) Du Rietz (CLH, 2 specimens from Mt. Washington); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in N.A
Cornutispora ciliata Kalb (St. Hilaire 2003); specimen in NY is only identified as Cornutispora sp.
Cresonea premnea (Ach.) Egea & Torrente (CLH, 8 19th century specimens); presumed misidentifications
Cryptolechia geoicoides (Vain.) Kalb (CLH, 1 Willey specimen from Bristol Co., MA, as Pachyphiale geoicoides); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021
Cyanisticta positiva Gyeln. (CLH, 1 specimen from CT det by Gyelnik); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021
Cyphelium viridescens (Lilj.) Vain. (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021
Cyrtidula hippocastani (DC.) R.C.Harris (CLH, 1 1896 MA specimen); presumed misidentification; specimen annotated as this species by Harris in 1974, but Harris 1995 states not in N.A.
Dendriscocaulon umhausense (Auersw.) Degel. (CLH, 8 specimens; Hinds & Hinds 1998); in N.E. a misapplied name for D. intricatulum
Dendrographa leucophaea (Tuck.) Darb. (CLH, 1 NH specimen from Mt. Washington at FH, det by R. Sundin in 1995); presumed location label error; far from distribution in coastal CA and Mexico
Dermatocarpon americanum Vain. (CLH, 1 specimen from VT annotated by S. Heiðmarsson as D. americanum in 1999); subsequent work by Amtoft et al. 2008 has cast doubt on this species occurring in eastern N.A.
Dermatocarpon polyphyllizum (Nyl.) Blomb. & Forssell (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution
Dermatocarpon reticulatum H.Magn. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in N.A. 
Dibaeis absoluta (Tuck.) Kalb & Gierl (CLH, 3 specimens, from northern Maine and 2500-3000’ elevation in VT); presumed misidentification, perhaps of Icmadaphila ericetorum; D. absoluta is a tropical lichen found as far north as southern Indiana and Ohio (Thomson 1967a)
Diploschistes diacapsis (Ach.) Lumbsch (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution
Dyplolabia afzelii (Ach.) A.Massal. (CLH, 1 specimen from NH); presumed misidentification; far from the rest of its distribution in SE NA
Endocarpon pallidum Ach. (CLH, 1 Merrill specimen from ME); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution; note on specimen says probably E. pusillum
Eopyrenula leucoplaca (Wallr.) R.C.Harris (CLH, 23 specimens); misidentifications for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Ephebe brasiliensis (Vain.) Henssen (CLH, 2 specimens); presumed misidentification; Henssen 1963a only cites specimens from Brazil 
Erioderma pedicellatum (Hue) P.M.Jørg. (Jørgensen 2000b, Maine); collection was from Campobello Island just off the Maine coast but which is part of New Brunswick, Canada
Evernia divaricata (L.) Ach. (CLH, 2 specimens); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution
Flavoparmelia rutidota (Hook. f. & Taylor) Hale (CLH, 1 Ryan specimen from VT at ASU); presumed misidentification; far from the rest of its range in SW US and Mexico 
Flavoplaca marina (Wedd.) Arup, Frödén & Søchting (CLH, 1 specimen from Maine coast (Taylor, 1965); also Degelius 1940); per Arup 1994, both are misidentifications of Flavoplaca microthallina
Fuscidea cyathoides (Ach.) V.Wirth & Vězda (CLH, 10 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Fuscidea kockiana (Hepp) V.Wirth & Vězda (CLH, 1 specimen); misidentification for N.A (Esslinger 2021)
Fuscidea mollis (Wahlenb.) Arnold (CLH, 1 specimen from MA); per Fryday 2008 all collections from northeastern N.A. are misidentifications, many of F. appalachensis Fryday
Fuscopannaria cyanolepra (Tuck.) P.M.Jørg. (CLH, 1 specimen from ME at SRP); identity uncertain; far from the rest of its distribution in western N.A.
Gabura fasciculare (L.) P.M.Jørg. (CLH, 1 Thaxter specimen from MA); presumed misidentification
Gowardia nigricans (Ach.) P.Halonen, L.Myllys, S.Velmala, & H.Hyvärinen (Eckfeldt 1894, ME, as Alectoria ochroleuca (Ehrh.) Nyl. var. nigricans Ach; Howe 1911, ME, as Alectoria nigricans (Ach.) Nyl., citing Eckfeldt; Fink 1935, ME, as Alectoria nigricans (Ach.) Nyl.); Eckfeldt’s specimen at FH is a mixture of Alectoria sarmentosa and Bryoria spp.
Graphis assimilis Nyl, (CLH, 1 Mann 1863 specimen from NH at UC); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution
Graphis intricata Fée (CLH, 2 Mann specimens from NH); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution
Gyalecta carneola (Ach.) Hellb. (CLH, 1 Frost specimens from VT); identity uncertain; needs to be examined as there are 2 recent records from N.A., from New Brunswick and Nova Scotia
Gyalecta geoica (Wahlenb. ex Ach.) Ach. (CLH, one Willey specimen at NY; Fink 1935, as Secoliga geoica); presumed misidentification from synonymizing G. geoica f. trivialis Willey with G. geoica instead of treating it as a separate species now known as Absconditella trivialis
Haematomma ochroleucum (Neck.) J.R.Laundon (CLH, 3 specimens); the actual label images show all were labeled as H. ochrophaeum, so they were digitized into CLH incorrectly 
Haematomma persoonii (Fée) A.Massal. (Parlin 1939, as H. puniceum); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in SE coastal plain southwards
Hazslinszkya gibberulosa (Ach.) Körb. (CLH, 1 specimen); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Heppia despreauxii (Mont.) Tuck. (CLH, 1 specimen); a misapplied name for H. adglutinata
Heterodermia casarettiana (A.Massal.) Trevis. (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain
Heterodermia comosa (Eschw.) Follm. & Redón (CLH, 1 specimen); presumeed misidentification; a tropical species (Kurokawa 1962); in N.A. most records are H. galactophylla (Esslinger 2021)
Heterodermia dendritica (Pers.) Poelt (CLH, 1 1934 specimen from ME); presumed misidentification; not included in Lendemer 2009a; most records are tropical
Heterodermia japonica (M.Satô) Swinscow & Krog (CLH, 2 specimens from same site collected by C. Cummings from northern ME); presumed misidentification; Lendemer 2009a reported the species as being restricted to extreme southeast in N.A. 
Heterodermia pseudospeciosa Kurok. (CLH, 2 specimens); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution further south
Hyperphyscia endochrysea (Nyl.) Filippini, Quiroga, J.M. Rodr. & Estrabou (CLH, 3 specimens); not in Esslinger 2021; in N.E. probably a misapplied name for Phaeophyscia rubropulchra
Hyperphyscia pyrithrocardia (Müll.Arg.) Moberg & Aptroot (Tuckerman 1882, as Physcia adglutinata * pyrithrocardia Müll.Arg., collected by Willey from MA); identification uncertain; Willey 1892 stated he was not able to find the species among his specimens; Thomson 1963 and Esslinger et al. 2012 did not list any US specimens except from FL and LA
Hypogymnia appalachensis Pike ex R.C.Harris (16 specimens in CLH); nom. inval. per Index Fungorum; probably within the normal variation of H. physodes (Hinds & Hinds 2007)
Hypogymnia enteromorpha (Ach.) Nyl. (CLH, 12 specimens; Degelius 1940, as Parmelia enteromorpha); misapplied name for Hypogymnia krogiae
Hypogymnia imshaugii Krog (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in western N.A.
Hypotrachyna caraccensis (Taylor) Hale (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification of this tropical species
Hypotrachyna imbricatula (Zahlbr.) Hale (CLH, 7 specimen); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in SE US
Hypotrachyna laevigata (Sm.) Hale (CLH, 3 specimens); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution
Hypotrachyna prolongata (Kurok.) Hale (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification
Hypotrachyna spumosa (Asahina) Krog & Swinscow (Lendemer & Harris 2004. as Parmelinopsis spumosa); later found to be Hypotrachyna showmanii
Hypotrachyna sublaevigata (Nyl. ex Tuck.) Hale (Fink 1935, as Parmelia sublaevigata Nyl.); 
Karstenia rhopaloides (Sacc.) Barel (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021 
Lasallia caroliniana (Tuck.) Davydov, Peršoh & Rambold (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; not found in N.E. in Llano 1950
Lasallia pustulata (L.) Mérat (48 specimens at CLH, Fink 1935, as Umbilicaria pustulata (L.) Hoffm.); presumed misidentification; not found in N.E. in Llano 1950, who found only two in N.A.; misapplied name for Lasallia papulosa
Lathagrium cristatum (L.) Otálora, P.M.Jørg. & Wedin (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain
Lecania nylanderiana A.Massal. (CLH, 2 Willey specimens); presumed misidentification; grows on limestone, which is scarce in NH and New Bedford, MA
Lecanographa lyncea (Sm.) Egea & Torrente (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in southwestern N.A.
Lecanora aitema (Ach.) Hepp (Willey 1892, as L. varia var. saepincola Fr.; Fink 1935, as Lecidea aitema); identity uncertain
Lecanora arthroocarpa Duby (Tuckerman 1882; Willey 1892); identity uncertain; not in Index Fungorum
Lecanora campestris (Schaer.) Hue (CLH, 11 specimens, Fink 1935); per Brodo 1984, in N.A. limited to CA
Lecanora carpinea (L.) Vain. (CLH, 2 specimens; Willey 1892, as L. pallida var. angulosa Hoffm.); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in N.A.
Lecanora coniza Tuck. (CLH, 1 Frost specimen from VT, holotype); Identity not certain; it has not been reported in N.A. since it was described; not in Tuckerman 1882
Lecanora elatina var. minor Tuck. (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain (Esslinger 2021)
Lecanora fulva (Anzi) Hamand (CLH, 1 Mann specimen); identity uncertain; no other N.A. records
Lecanora horiza (Ach.) Lindsay (CLH, 2 specimens, Evans & Meyrowitz 1926); presumed misidentification; most of distribution centered in CA
Lecanora impudens (CLH, 14 specimens; Sullivan 1996); status uncertain; most or all are probably L. appalachensis (Lendemer et al. 2013)
Lecanora miculata Ach. (CLH, 2 specimens, both from ME at the same site, and both determined by C.Dodge); identity uncertain, but given Dodge’s reputation for identification errors, it seems best to exclude this generally SE US species.
Lecanora microfusca (CLH, 1 specimen from Mt. Washington, NH); presumed misidentification; a rare species from the high arctic that grows on calcareous rock, which is not known to occur on Mt. Washington
Lecanora orosthea (Ach.) Ach. (CLH, 12 records, the most recent 1910; Tuckerman 1882; Willey 1892; Fink 1935, who cites L. expallens as a synonym); identity uncertain, no recent records in N.A.
Lecanora populicola (DC.) Duby (CLH, 4 specimens latest 1921); presumed misidentification; no recent specimens in eastern NA
Lecanora substrobilina Printzen (CLH, 1 specimen at US from ME); presumed misidentification; rest of N.A. distribution is on west coast
Lecanora subtartarea Nyl. (Merrill 1911, Maine); identity uncertain; not known to occur in N.A.
Lecanora varia (Hoffm.) Ach. (CLH, 266 specimens, but none since 1980; Hale 1950); identity uncertain; formerly used much more broadly to include several species
Lecanora verruculosa Jatta (CLH, 1 19th century specimen); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 1921
Lecidea atrorubens Fr. (CLH, 4 Merrill exsiccati specimens); identity uncertain; only N.A. records are these four from ME
Lecidea ceroplasta (C.Bab.) Hook. f. (CLH, 1 Frost specimen); presumed misidentification of this species found in New Zealand and Australia
Lecidea convexa (Fr.) Th.Fr. (CLH, 10 specimens all from the same location in ME); identity uncertain
Lecidea elegans (Hepp ex A.Massal.) Stizenb. (CLH, 3 specimens); identity uncertain
Lecidea enteroleuca auct. (CLH, 21 specimens); identity uncertain
Lecidea exigua Chaub. (CLH, 7 specimens, all 1800s); identify uncertain; no recent collections in N.A.
Lecidea extenuata Vain. (CLH, 1 Willey specimen); identity uncertain; no other collections anywhere near New England.
Lecidea katahdinensis Degel. (Degelius 1940: Katahdin, 1400 m, on rock); per pers. comm. from Alan Fryday (and he with Måns Svensson), probably an immature Porpidia macrocarpa
Lecidea lithophila (Ach.) Ach. (CLH, 4 specimens from early 20th century); identity uncertain
Lecidea morio (Duby) Fr. (Tuckerman 1888); identity uncertain (Esslinger 2021)
Lecidea peliaspis (Tuck.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 8 specimens from N.E. and 28 specimens from N.A., but only one collected in the 20th century); may be a misapplied name for Lecidea albofuscescens Nyl. (Lowe 1939)
Lecidea ramulosa Th.Fr. (CLH, 1 MA specimen); presumed misidentification of this arctic alpine species
Lecidea rivulorum H.Magn.(CLH, 1 Evans specimen at YU, E. Hampton CT, a duplicate of the holotype at UPS); no other records in N.A.; per Alan Fryday and Måns Svensson, probably a synonym of Bryobilimbia ahlesii
ecidella parasema (Ach.) Arnold (CLH, 4 specimens; Fink 1935 as Lecidea parasema); identity uncertain; no recent records
Lepra albescens (Huds.) Hafellner (CLH, 7 specimens, 1 recent); identity uncertain; per Dibben 1980, all eastern N.A. records have proved to be other species
Lepra commutata (Müll.Arg.) Lendemer & R.C.Harris (CLH, 1 19th century specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in SE N.A.
Lepra hypothamnolica (Dibben) Lendemer & R.C.Harris (CLH, 1 ME specimen); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in SE US
Lepra submultipuncta (Nyl.) Q.Ren (CLH, 1 specimen labeled Pertusaria submultipuncta); presumed misidentification; Dibben (1980) states it is a Japanese endemic
Lepraria gracilescens (Nyl.) Lendemer & Hodkinson (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in western N.A.
Lepraria incana (L.) Ach. (CLH, 10 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Lepraria lobificans auct.N.A. non Nyl. (CLH, 102 specimens); not in N.A.per Lendemer 2013
Lepraria nivalis J.R.Laundon (CLH, 5 specimens); presumed misidentification; per Lendemer 2013, in eastern N.A. a misapplied name for L. normandinoides
Leptogium azureum (Sw. ex Ach.) Mont. (CLH, 1 specimen, CT, 1884); identify uncertain; reported to be a mixture of L. cyanescens and L. azureum, but non-isidate portions of L. cyanescens can be confused with L. azureum
Leptogium britannicum P.M.Jørg. & P.James (CLH, 1 specimen, VT, 1922, det G.K.Merrill); presumed misidentification; no other N.A. records of this species known
Leptogium burgessii (L.) Mont. (Fink 1935); per Sierk 1964, a misapplied name for L. americanum (now L. laceroides)
Leptogium burnetiae C.W.Dodge (CLH, 1 specimen); formerly thought to be as a synonym for L. hirsutum, now considered a misidentification for N.A. (Stone et al. 2016)
Leptogium denticulatum Nyl. (CLH, 1 specimen); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Leptogium hildenbrandii (Garov.) Nyl. (CLH, 1 specimen); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Leptogium saturninum (Dicks.) Nyl. (CLH, 51 specimens; Tuckerman 1882, Hinds & Hinds 2007, and many others); per Stone et al. 2016, it is not found in eastern N.A.; reports in eastern N.A. are L. acadiense (or L. hirsutum)
Lithoicea subvirens M.Choisy (CLH, 1 Willey MA specimen); identity uncertain, perhaps Verrucaria glaucovirens
Lithothelium illotum (Nyl.) Aptroot (CLH, 1 Green specimen from 1895); misreading of label handwriting: could be Chester SC, not Chester ME
Lobaria anthraspis (Ach.) T.Sprib. & McCune (Fink 1935, as Sticta anthraspis); presumed misidentification
Lobaria linita (Ach.) Rabenh. (CLH, 3 specimens; Fink 1935); presumed misidentification of this high arctic and western species
Lopadium pezizoideum (CLH, 58 records); presumed misidentifications; per Brodo et al. 2001, L. pezizoideum is an arctic/alpine species growing on moss or dead vegeation, not on bark, and none of the ones from N.E. in CLH were collected in appropriate habitat and substrate
Maronea constans (Nyl.) Hepp (CLH, 19 records); presumed misidentification; per Brodo 2016, N.A. records except in southern Appalachians are M. polyphaea
Massalongia carnosa (Dicks.) Körb. (CLH, 1 specimen from ME); presumed misidentification; not in arctic, boreal, or alpine habitat
Megalaria intermixta (Nyl.) Kalb (CLH, 1 specimen, as Biatorina intermixta (Nyl.) Kieff.); presumed misidentification; not in Esslinger 2021
Megalospora pachycheila (Tuck.) Sipman (CLH, 1 Willey specimen); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in SE coastal plain 
Megalospora tuberculosa (Fée) Sipman (CLH, 8 19th century collections); presumed misidentifications; far from rest of distribution in NA in SE coastal plain
Melanelixia californica A.Crespo & Divakar (CLH, 1 specimen, as Melanelia glabra); presumed misidentification: a western N.A. species
Melanelixia fuliginosa (Fr. ex Duby) O.Blanco et al. (CLH, 87 specimens); misidentification of P. glabratula (Esslinger 2021) 
Melaspilea enteroleuca (Ach.) Ertz & Diederich (CLH, 21 specimens, as Lecidea enteroleuca); identity uncertain
Melaspilea lentiginosula (Nyl.) A.L.Sm. (CLH, 1 specimen); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Microthelia willeyana Müll.Arg. (CLH, 3 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Mycoblastus sanguinarius (L.) Norman (CLH, 430 specimens); status uncertain; most are likely to be M. sanguinarioides (Brodo 2016), but without close examination, the identity of most will remain uncertain 
Naetrocymbe atomarioides (Müll.Arg.) R.C.Harris (CLH, 4 specimens); MA specimens at NY are from Florida, not MA, and YU specimen has “Not Conn.” written on the packet
Naetrocymbe rhyponta (Ach.) R.C.Harris (Willey 1892 and CLH report an 1881 MA specimen labeled Pyrenula rhyponta (Ach.) Hepp); Harris 1995 states that “no ‘good’ American material seen”
Nesolechia cladoniscum (Willey) Fink (CLH, 2 specimens); apothecia of Pycnothelia papillaria (Esslinger 2021)
Nesolechia papillariae (Willey) Fink (CLH, 2 specimens); apothecia of Pycnothelia papillaria (Esslinger 2021)
Ochrolechia farinacea G.E.Howard (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; all other specimens from the Pacific Northwest
Ochrolechia pallescens (L.) A.Massal. (CLH, 44 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Ochrolechia parella (L.) A.Massal. (CLH, 11 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Ochrolechia subviridis (Høeg) Erichsen (CLH, 2 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)

Opegrapha leucoplaca Müll.Arg. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in SE US
Ophioparma lapponica (Räsänen) Hafellner & R.W.Rogers (CLH, 20 specimens); presumed misidentifications; May 1998b has determined that O. lapponica and O. ventosa are best separated by spore septation not chemistry, and on that basis all Ophioparma species in N.E. are O. ventosa
Pannaria pannosa (Sw.) Nyl. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification
Parmelina coleae Argüello & A.Crespo (CLH, 14 specimens) ; in N.E. a misapplied name for Myelochroa galbina
Parmelina quercina (Willd.) Hale (CLH, 11 specimens); in N.E. a misapplied name for Myelochroa galbina
Parmelina tiliacea (Hoffm.) Hale (CLH, 75 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Parmotrema cetratum (Ach.) Hale (CLH, 23 specimens, all but 3 from before 1940, Tuckerman 1882, Willey 1892, Fink 1935); identity uncertain: formerly the name included the more common sorediate species, P. reticulatum; one recently collected specimen with this name, 1999 from Middlesex Co., MA
Parmotrema nilgherrense (Nyl.) Hale (CLH, 1 Merrill specimen from ME); presumed misidentification; not accepted by Esslinger 2021; mostly an African and Asian species
Parmotrema subcaperatum (Kremp.) Hale (CLH, 1 Willey specimen det A.Spielman 2008); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021; reported from Mexico to S. America and Australia
Parmotrema subrugatum (Kremp.) Hale (Willey 1892); presumed misidentification of this tropical lichen
Parmotrema ultralucens (Krog) Hale (CLH, 1 specimen); probably a misidentification (B. Goffinet, pers. comm.) 
Parmotrema xanthinum (Müll.Arg.) Hale (CLH, 7 specimens); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in SE US 
Pertusaria flavicunda Tuck. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; a SW N.A. species
Pertusarria glomerata (Ach.) Schaer. (CLH, 27 records, all 1987 or before); presumed misidentification; per Dibben 1980, misapplied name for P. subobducens
Pertusaria hymenea (Ach.) Schaer. (CLH, 50 records, none recent); per Dibben 1980, not present in eastern N.A.
Pertusaria multipuncta (Turner) Nyl. (CLH, 87 specimens, Tuckerman 1882, Fink 1935); presumed misidentification; N.A. species resembling P. multipuncta separated as P. multipunctoides by Dibben 1980
Pertusaria oculata (Dicks.) Th.Fr. (CLH, 2 specimens, a Frost specimen from 1852 and one identified by Dibben as Ochrolechia inaequatula); presumed misidentification
Pertusaria pertusa (Weigel) Tuck.(CLH, 106 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Phacographa glaucomaria (Nyl.) Hafellner (Fink 1935, as Leciographa glaucomaria, MA); identity uncertain
Phaeocalicium tremulicola (Norrl. ex Nyl.) Tibell (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; on wrong substrate per Selva 2014
Phaeographis dendritica (Ach.) Müll.Arg. (CLH, 43 specimens in N.E.; Willey 1892, Fink 1935); identity uncertain; many and perhaps all of these specimens may be a misapplied name for Phaeographis inusta (Körb.) Moberg
Phaeophyscia constipata (Norrl. & Nyl.) Moberg (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of N.A. distribution in arctic and western alpine
Phaeophyscia endococcina (Körb.) Moberg (CLH, 8 specimens); presumed misidentifications; per Esslinger 1978 reports of this species in N.A. are misidentifications of P. endcoccinodes
Phaeorrhiza nimbosa (H.Mayrhofer) Poelt (CLH, 2 specimens from one site); should be Mt. Garfield in CO not NH 
Physcia albinea (Ach.) Nyl. (CLH, 3 specimens from two sites); identity uncertain
Physcia atrostriata (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain: far from rest of distribution in SE US
Physcia clementei (CLH, 4 specimens named P. astroidea); presumed misidentification; per Brodo 2016 ; in N.A. a southern species 
Physcia insularis (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification
Physconia distorta (With.) J.R.Laundon (CLH, 32 specimens); misidentification for N.A.(Esslinger 2021)
Physconia grisea (Lam.) Poelt (CLH, 54 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Physconia isidiigera (Zahlbr.) Essl. (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain
Placidium lachneum (Ach.) Breuss (CLH, 6 specimens, Fink 1935); probably a misapplied name for P. squamulosum
Placidium rufescens (Ach.) A.Massal. (Fink 1935); presumed misidentification of P. squamulosum
Platismatia lacunosa (Ach.) W.L.Culb. & C.F.Culb. (CLH, 124 specimens; Willey 1892); presumed misidentification; now understood to be a western species in N. A. 
Platismatia stenophylla (Tuck.) W.L.Culb. & C.F.Culb. (CLH, 5 specimens); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in western N.A.
Polycauliona candelaria (L.) Frödén (CLH, 106 specimens; Willey 1892, as Theloschistes lychneus); presumed misidentifications; most are misapplied name for Xanthomendoza weberi
Polymeridium subcinereum (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in SE N.A.
Porina cembricola (Anzi) Lettau (CLH, 1 Willey MA specimen); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021
Porina olivacea (Pers.) A.L.Sm. (CLH, 5 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Porina pulla (Ach.) Müll.Arg (CLH, 1 specimen); an Arthopyrenia species not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Porpidia hydrophila (Fr.) Hertel & A.J.Schwab (CLH, 7 specimens); identity uncertain 
Protoblastenia calva (Dicks.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 1 specimen from VT); presumed misidentification
Pseudephebe minuscula (Nyl. ex Arnold) Brodo & D.Hawksw. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification
Pseudephebe pubescens (L.) M.Choisy (21 specimens in CLH, as Ephebe pubescens or Alectoria pubescens); as used by N.E. collectors, a misapplied name for Ephebe lanata; no true P. pubescens known in N.E.
Pseudevernia furfuracea (L.) Zopf (CLH, 11 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021) ; N.E. records are P. consocians 
Pseudocyphellaria crocata (L.) Vain. (CLH, 127 specimens; Hinds & Hinds 1998; Hinds & Hinds 2007); misidentifications for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Pseudocyphellaria perpetua McCune & Miądl. (CLH, 6 specimens; Hinds & Hinds 2007); %% P. hawaiiensis, but in N.E., a misapplied name (Esslinger 2021)
Psora russellii (Tuck.) A.Schneid. (CLH, 45 specimens with that name in N.E.); per Timdal 1986, specimens with that name in northeastern NA are Psora pseudorussellii
Punctelia borreri (Sm.) Krog (CLH, 27 specimens, most from 19th century; Fink 1935, as Parmelia borreri); in N.E., a misapplied name for P. caseana
Punctelia hypoleucites (Nyl.) Krog (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in central and western US and Mexico.
Punctelia perreticulata (Räsänen) G.Wilh. & Ladd (CLH, 22 specimens; Hinds & Hinds 2007); presumed misidentification; per Lendemer & Hodkinson 2010, this name is now restricted to a species with a range concentrated in the Ozarks
Punctelia reddenda (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain
Punctelia subrudecta (Nyl.) Krog (CLH, 48 records; Hinds & Hinds 1998); per Lendemer & Hodkinson 2010, in N.E. these are all P. caseana
Pyrenocarpon thelostomum (Ach. ex J.Harrriman) Coppins & Aptroot (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain
Pyrenopsis corallina Willey (CLH, 4 specimens; Tuckerman 1882); identity uncertain (Esslinger 2021)
Pyrenula aspistea (Afzel. ex Ach.) Ach. (Willey 1892; Fink 1935); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in N.A.
Pyrenula cruenta (Mont.) Vain. (CLH, 1 NH specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of N.A. distribution in SE
Pyrenula mamillana (Ach.) Trevis. (CLH, 1 Willey speciman); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in SE N.A.
Pyrenula nitida (Weigel) Ach. (CLH, 83 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Pyrenula ravenelii (Tuck.) R.C. Harris (CLH, a 1946 specimen froms Cape Cod); identity uncertain
Ramalina calicaris (L.) Fr. (CLH, 109 specimens; Tuckerman 1882; Willey 1892; Fink 1935); in N.E., presumed misidentification; formerly used for a species now known as R. americana
Ramalina fastigiata (Pers.) Ach. (CLH, 78 specimens; Tuckerman 1882, Willey 1892; Fink 1935); in N.E. presumed misidentification; formerly used for a species now known as R. americana
Ramalina fraxinea (L.) Ach. (CLH, 12 specimens; Tuckerman 1882, Willey 1892, Fink 1935); in N.E. presumed misidentification; formerly used for a species now known as R. americana
Ramalina geniculata Hooke f. & Taylor (CLH, 1 Tuckerman specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in N.A.
Ramalina hypoprotocetrarica W.L.Culb. (CLH, 3 specimens); for purposes of this checklist, considered conspecific with R. farinacea
Ramalina inflata (f. & Taylor) Hook. f. & Taylor (CLH, 3 specimens); in N.E. presumed misidentification of R. roesleri or R. dilacerata; 
Ramalina montagnei De Not (CLH, 2 specimens); presumed misidentification; far from rest of distribution in SE US
Ramalina peruviana Ach. (CLH, 1 specimen from NH); presumed misidentification; far from rest of its distribution in NA in southern states 
Ramalina polymorpha Ach. (CLH, 4 specimens; Fink 1935); presumed misidentification
Ramalina sinensis Jatta (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain; far from most of distribution further west
Ramalina stenospora Müll.Arg. (CLH, 1 specimen); identified by S.LaGreca as R. americana
Ramalina subamplicata (Nyl.) Fink [in Fink 1935 as 'subamplicata'] %% Ramalina calicaris (Index Fungorum), but see Excluded Species list
Ramalina subfraxinea Nyl. (Willey 1892, Fink 1935); presumed misidentification
Ramalina tenuis (Tuck.) G.Merr. (CLH, 5 specimens); a misapplied name for R. willeyi (Howe 1914b) 
Ramalina usnea (L.) R.Howe (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification
Rhizocarpon ferax H.Magn. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; S. LaGreca examined the specimen and thinks it probably is R. lecanorinum
Rhizocarpon obscuratum (Ach.) A.Massal (CLH, 41 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger2021)
Rhizocarpon plicatile auct. N.A. (CLH, 13 specimens); a misapplied name, most often for R. rubescens
Rhizocarpon richardii (Lamy ex Nyl.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 16 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Rhizocarpon riparium Räsänen (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain
Rhizocarpon tinei Runemark (CLH, 4 NH specimens from Alpine Garden of Mt. Washington collected in 1894); identity uncertain; not included in Esslinger 2021 
Ricasolia amplissima (Scop.) DeNot. (CLH, 66 specimens; Tuckerman 1882 and Fink 1935, as Sticta amplissima); in eastern N.A. most are a misapplied name for Ricasolia (Lobaria) quercizans, but a few are misapplied name for Dendriscocaulon intricatulum
Ricasolia virens (With.) Blomb & Tønsberg (CLH, 4 specimens); not in N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Rinodina archaea (Ach.) Arnold (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain; Sheard 2010 reports the species only from western N.A.
Rinodina atrocinerea (Hook.) Körb. (CLH, 4 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Rinodina confragosa (Ach.) Körb. (CLH, 2 specimens; Willey 1892, Fink 1935, LaGreca et al. 2005); presumed misidentification; Sheard 2010 states this species is not found in eastern N.A.
Rinodina exigua (Ach.) Gray (CLH, 25 specimens; Willey 1892, Fink 1935); presumed misidentifications; per Sheard 2010, in N.A. restricted to CA
Rinodina milvina (Wahlenb.) Th.Fr. (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in western N.A. (Sheard 2010)
Rinodina sophodes (Ach.) A.Massal (CLH, 34 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Sarcogyne lapponica (Ach. ex Schaer.) K.Knudsen & Kocourk (CLH, 5 specimens); misidentifications per annotation by K.Knudsen
Sclerococcum luridum (Hafellner) Ertz & Diederich (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; annotatated by R.C.Harris with a ?
Sclerococcum saxatile (Schaer.) Ertz & Diederich (Tuckerman 1888, as Buellia saxatilis); based on the species this fungus is parasitizing (Baeomyces rufus), it is more likely that it is Sclerococcum athallina 
Sporostigma melasporum (Tuck.) Grube (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of N.A. distribution in Florida.
Stereocaulon evolutum Graewe: (CLH, 2 specimens); not on N.A. checklist and a presumed misidentification
Stereocaulon subintricans Nyl: (CLH, 2 specimens); identified as S. subintricans by I.Lamb, who noted it was a doubtful species
Sticta herbacea (Huds.) Ach. (CLH, 4 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Sticta sylvatica (Huds.) Ach. (CLH, 2 19th century specimens; Fink 1935); presumed misidentification (see Hodkinson et al. 2014)
Strigula smaragdula Fr. (CLH, 1 specimen); specimen is from South America not MA
Trypethelium mastoideum (Ach.) Ach. (CLH, 2 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Tuckermannopsis chlorophylla (Fink 1935, as Cetraria chlorophylla, New England); presumed misidentification, although there are recent records in Nova Scotia and Quebec
Tuckermannopsis platyphylla (Tuck.) Gyeln. (CLH, 3 specimens); presumed misidentification; far from rest of disttibution in western N.A.
Umbilicaria angulata Tuck. (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification, not found in N.E. in Llano 1950
Umbilicaria arctica (Ach.) Nyl. (CLH, 2 specimens; Fink 1935, as Gyrophora arctica); presumed misidentification, not found in N.E. in Llano 1950
Umbilicaria decussata (Vill.) Zahlbr. (Fink 1935, as Gyrophora decussata (Vill.) Zahlbr.); per Llano 1950 a misidentification of U. hyperborea
Umbilicaria grisea Hoffm. (CLH, 26 specimens); misidentification for N.A. (Esslinger 2021)
Umbilicaria phaea Tuck. (2 specimens in CLH); presumed misidentification, not found in N.E. in Llano 1950
Umbilicaria pustulata (L.) Hoffm. (CLH, 104 specimens, Tuckerman 1882, Willey 1892, Fink 1935); per Llano 1950, extremely rare in N.A. with none in N.E.; a misapplied name for U. papulosa 
Usnea articulata (L.) Hoffm. (CLH, 1 specimen); specimen was from UK
Usnea deformis Motyka (CLH, 1 Tuckerman specimen); identity uncertain
Usnea dolosa Motyka (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain
Usnea fastigiata Motyka (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain
Usnea florida (L.) Weber ex F.H.Wigg. (CLH, 207 specimens, Tuckerman 1848, Evans & Meyrowitz 1926, Fink 1935); a misapplied name for U. strigosa
Usnea geniculata (Hook. f. & Taylor) Bowler & Rundel (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; far from rest of its distribution
Usnea intermedia (A.Massal.) Jatta (CLH, three 19th century specimens det J.Motyka 1938); presumed misidentification; per Clerc 2007 a species of western N.A. and Europe
Usnea linearis A.Schneid. (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain
Usnea maxima Motyka (CLH, 1 specimen annotated by A.Herre); identity uncertain
Usnea plicata (L.) Weber ex F.H.Wigg.
Usnea scholanderi Llano (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain
Variospora velana (A.Massal.) Arup, Søchting & Frödén (Hinds et al. 2009, as Caloplaca velana); per Brodo 2016, this name may or may not be synonymous with Squamulea subsoluta, so it will be excluded until further work is done on this question
Verrucaria aquatilis Mudd (CLH, 1 Merrill specimen); identity uncertain
Verrucaria caerulea DC. [also spelled coerulea] (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain
Verrucaria ceuthocarpa Wahlenb. (Willey 189, MA: Fink 1935, ME and MA); identity uncertain; the Willey report may have been V. degelii, a species not described until 1939 which looks very similar to V. ceuthocarpa (Taylor 1982); the Fink report for ME may be a location error, confusing collections from Grand Manan I., NB as collections from ME.
Verrucaria dolomitica (A.Massal.) Kremp. (CLH, 3 specimens from one site in VT); identity uncertain; no other sites in eastern N.A., but recently reported in Montana (McCune et al. 2014)
Verrucaria funckii (Spreng.) Zahlbr. (CLH, 1 1995 specimen from VT); identity uncertain; spore size appears to be too small for V. funckii
Verrucaria internigrescens (Nyl.) Erichsen (CLH, 1 1998 specimen from Boston Islands); identity uncertain; not listed in the LaGreca et al. 2005 paper on Boston Islands lichens and bryophytes
Verrucaria ochrostoma Borrer (CLH, 2 Merrill specimens from ME); identity uncertain
Verrucaria rupestris Schrad. (CLH, 27 specimens; all before 1949; Fink 1935); identity uncertain; most and perhaps all N.E. records of V. rupestris are V. muralis, which Fink 1935 considered a synonym of V. rupestris
Verrucaria subfuscella Nyl. (CLH, 1 Pringle specimen); identity uncertain; not in Esslinger 2021
Verrucaria submersella (CLH, 1 Evans specimen); identity uncertain; Evans & Meyrowitz 1926 cites this specimen as V. submersa, which is synonym of V. hydrela, but V. submersa is not known to be a synonym of V. submersella
Vulpicida canadensis (Räsänen) J.-E.Mattsson & M.J.Lai (CLH, 19 specimens); presumed misapplied name for V. pinastri
Vulpicida juniperinum (L.) J.-E.Mattsson & M.J.Lai (CLH, 21 specimens); presumed misaplied name for V. viridis or V. pinastri
Vulpicida platyphylla (Tuck.) Hale (CLH, 6 specimens); presumed misidentification
Xanthocarpia lactea (A.Massal.) A.Massal. (CLH, 4 specimens from MA); presumed misidentification; per Vondrák et al. 2011, this is a mediterranean and sub-meditrerranean European species 
Xanthomendoza fulva (Hoffm.) Søchting, Kärnefelt & S.Y.Kondr. (CLH, 12 specimens); per Lindblom 2006, all specimens with this name in eastern N.A. are X. weberi
Xanthoparmelia australasica D.J.Galloway (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; rare in N.A. per Nash & Elix 2004
Xanthoparmelia isidiosa (Jatta) Elix & J.Johnst. (CLH, 1 specimen, identified by Hale in 1953); identification uncertain; not in Hale 1990 as a N.A. species
Xanthoparmelia lineola (E.C.Berry) Hale (CLH, 1 specimen); identification uncertain; far from rest of distribution in western N.A.
Xanthoparmelia mexicana (Gyeln.) Hale (CLH 2 specimens); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribution in N.A.
Xanthoparmelia neotaractica Hale (CLH, 1 specimen); identity uncertain; far from rest of distribuyion in N.A.
Xanthoparmelia pulla (Ach.) O.Blanco, A.Crespo, Elix, D.Hawksw. & Lumbsch (CLH, 4 old specimens); presumed misidentification; misapplied name for Montanelia panniformis
Xanthoparmelia stenophylla (Ach.) Ahti & D.Hawksw. (CLH, 143 specimens); some of these are older collections using this name, and some arise because herbaria follow Ahti & Hawksworth 2005, who state that X. somloënsis should now be called X. stenophylla; rather than Lendemer 2005 who says that eastern N.A. specimens called X. somloënsis should now be called X. viriduloumbrina
Xanthoparmelia verruculifera (Nyl.) O.Blanco, A.Crespo, Elix, D.Hawksw. & Lumbsch (CLH, 7 specimens, Knox Co. ME, all Merrill’s Lich. Exs. #232, as Parmelia verruculifera); presumed misidentification; in N.A. a western species
Xanthoparmelia wyomingica (Gyeln.) Hale (CLH, 1 specimen); presumed misidentification; a western N.A. soil lichen
Xanthoria substellaris (Ach.) Vain. (CLH, 2 specimens); identity uncertain
